  2. I use this in addition to coconut oil ask a mask (I am currently transitioning to natural hair and using only natural products). It helps with moisture because my hair gets dry easily.
  3. I have dry brittle hair and have been using coconut oil for years. I decided to try out JBCO just out of curiosity and I am impressed by the results. If you are new to JBCO, here's a few things you might want to keep in mind:<br />1. The smell- thousands of users will tell you that castor oil smells terrible. I personally find the odor similar to petroleum jelly (thats the best I can come up with). I found the odor light and not at all unpleasant. However, if you are very sensitive to smell, you should test the real thing before buying.<br /><br />2. Consistency- JBCO is thick, very thick. I put a tiny amount in a bowl, add few drops of coconut/olive oil to ensure it can penetrate the scalp, dip my fingers into the mixture and massage it into my scalp. Yes, it takes a little more time and effort than other hair oils, but I think its worth it. The problem with viscous oils is, you feel as though you need a lot more to cover the scalp, then you overdo it and then it is harder to wash off. So, at least for the first couple of uses, go easy on the quantity and you can increase it later.<br /><br />3. Surprisingly easy to wash off. I was expecting trouble, but after leaving it on for 2 hours, my scalp had absorbed most of it.<br /><br />4. The effects- My hair grows pretty fast naturally, so I cannot comment on whether JBCO helped in that aspect or not. However, hair is definitely shinier, healthier and split ends are under control. Interestingly, I never realized that using this product could add volume to my thin and limp hair! That was a pleasant surprise :-)<br /><br />Normally, I use shampoo, wash-off conditioner, leave-in conditioner/scalp treatment and of course oiling. But now, I am using only JBCO and shampoo, as my hair does not need anything else. It is manageable. I like the fact that my hair is no longer exposed to tons of gunk from several products. And the wallet is happier too ;-)<br /><br />A word of advice for the newbies-<br />1. From what I have read,the success of JBCO is subjective. People (including me) tout it as a miracle product, but not everyone benefits from it. So, it might not be the holy grail of haircare for everyone.<br />2. I could leave in coconut oil in my hair overnight, but I have never done so with JBCO, primarily because I am worried that it might be too heavy for skin. In the past I have had facial acne due to hair products, so I am a little paranoid.<br /><br />I think I am gonna stick with it.

  127. There are a few things I want to clear up about this product. I used the whole bottle last year and am done with it. I switched to coconut oil to try something different but I would like to start using another JBCO castor oil on my hair. I didn't have any bad experiences with this when using it. But I see a LOT of people on here saying how it causes severe itching, head aches, shedding etc. The severe itching comes from when you put too much on your scalp. I made the mistake of doing that one day. Putting too much JBCO on my scalp and hair and let me tell you it was itching so bad that week until I washed it out. Once I washed it out there was no more itching. Then I started using it twice a week and not putting so much in such a little time on my hair and scalp and no itching. People also say it causes headaches. Again you are probably using too much and that is another side effect of putting too much JBCO on your hair and scalp in such a short time period. I see some people saying they put it on 4-6 times a week. I would say you should put this on at least 2-3 times a week. It's not going to make it grow any faster by putting too much on it. And yes this stuff is very thick and greasy. So you really only want to put a little on your hair unless you like that mucky feel and look. As for shedding I never experienced that either. Again putting too much on your hair could be causing it to shed. And lastly the smell. I had heard people saying how the smell of this stuff is overwhelming but when I got it and sniffed it I actually couldn't smell anything. Now when I started using it down then I could smell it and it smelled like ashes. But to me it wasn't a bad smell or overwhelming. But what do you expect to happen when you look at the ingredients in this. If you don't like the smell I'd suggest buying the lavender, coconut oil JBCO, etc. If you want good hair growing results I also suggest switching to organic shampoos and conditioners, take LOTS of vitamins especially biotin, prenatal pills etc, and find good hair creams to use. When my hair broke off from the breast reduction surgery I had I did research on what vitamins I need to take, the kind of shampoos and conditioners to use, and what are some good oils to use to aid in hair growth. Now granted any product you use there could be negative side effects you experience but you have to take in consideration of using things in moderation and not going overboard because you want fast hair growth. I relax my hair and I usually relax it every 2 or 2 1/2 months because that's how fast it grows. And in between I usually get about 4 or so inches of new growth. Right now I am on crappy chemo which thins my hair and makes it more prone to shedding and breakage. Plus I am anemic which also can make your hair thin and prone to breakage. And before my surgery my hair was long and thick down to my shoulders and then capoot I had to start over. So you also may want to make sure you don't have any underlying medical conditions that aid in shedding and breakage.biotin, prenatal pills etc, and find good hair creams to use. Our scalps have not been itchy since applying the product and the stickiness isn't an issue because I added this to a homemade hair grease/pomade (at least 4 capfuls to about 14oz of hair cream.<br /><br />I'm not going to mention all the ingredients, but to give you an idea, my homemade hair creams and body salves are made of natural oils, such as virgin coconut oil, extra virgin olive oil, unrefined avocado oil, jojoba, a few nut oils, true ivory unrefined shea butter(softened by stirring with a fork, NOT MELTED!!), calendula essential oil, tea tree essential oil, myrrh, ylang ylang extra...you get the idea, all natural ingredients. For the summer only, I added about 6 drops of vegetable glycerine to it to pull moisture out of the air and into our hair. Don't do that in Winter because the air is dry from the heaters and furnaces being on and it will pull the moisture out of your scalp and the inside of your hair to moisturize the outside of your strand, which will quickly cause damage and breakage. Vegetable glycerine is great for moisturizing during humid months.<br /><br />Also, I don't get what the big fuss is about the smell. It doesn't smell good or bad to me and since it's mixed into a hair dressing when I apply it, I don't smell it afterward in my or my daughter's hair.<br /><br />I will say, that I also bought the same brand JBCO Hair food, which has a much more pungeant smell/odor than this oil. I added some of this JBCO to it as well and applied that to our hair and scalp. We still don't see what is offensive about the scent and I can barely if at all smellit once it's in our hair. My suggestion, is that one could add a good essential oil to the bottle to tweak the smell. I'd only put up to 6 drops though for such a small bottle. Essential oils are powerful with wonderful benefits but could make you sick if not diluted well. Always remember that essential oils can be diluted with oil only, so if you spill some or use it too concentrated on the skin or scalp, take coconut, olive, any vegetable or carrier oil will do to clean it off. Water won't do any good because essential oils are oil soluble. Wash it off with the vegetable/carrier oil, then wash that off with soap and water. Another suggestion, is that this brand of JBCO is also sold in scented varieties. The only one I've seen so far is Lavender. It's supposedly slightly thinner in consistency, but people seem to like it and it smells good, so the reviews say (I haven't and don't plan on trying it, I'm satisfied with this original).<br /><br />If you're going to add essential oil to this JBCO, I recommend calendula, blood orange, lavender...something with a nice scent. You could use fragrant oils manufactured exclusively for fragrancing cosmetics/soaps/candles and the like, but I wouldn't go that route unless you can find some made with plant oils and extracts instead of synthetic chemicals and no, I am not talking about body oils that you wear like perfume. I guess you could but I personally would not.<br /><br />Anyway, I liked the way our homemade hair dressing and the Tropical Isle Living JBCO Hair Food worked before, but adding the JBCO to them seemed to increase the results of what we were looking for: shine, manageability, softening, sealing and growth.<br /><br />This oil seems fine to me and I plan to buy much more of it.
